      '\n' +
      'binfmt_misc restore write access before closing files opened by open_exec()\n' +
      '\n' +
      'bm_register_write() opens an executable file using open_exec(), which\n' +
      'internally calls do_open_execat() and denies write access on the file to\n' +
      'avoid modification while it is being executed.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'However, when an error occurs, bm_register_write() closes the file using\n' +
      'filp_close() directly. This does not restore the write permission, which\n' +
      'may cause subsequent write operations on the same file to fail.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Fix this by calling exe_file_allow_write_access() before filp_close() to\n' +
      'restore the write permission properly. | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

      '\n' +
      'ipv4 route Prevent rt_bind_exception() from rebinding stale fnhe\n' +
      '\n' +
      "The sit driver's packet transmission path calls sit_tunnel_xmit() ->\n" +
      'update_or_create_fnhe(), which lead to fnhe_remove_oldest() being called\n' +
      'to delete entries exceeding FNHE_RECLAIM_DEPTH+random.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The race window is between fnhe_remove_oldest() selecting fnheX for\n' +
      'deletion and the subsequent kfree_rcu(). During this time, the\n' +
      "concurrent path's __mkroute_output() -> find_exception() can fetch the\n" +
      'soon-to-be-deleted fnheX, and rt_bind_exception() then binds it with a\n' +
      'new dst using a dst_hold(). When the original fnheX is freed via RCU,\n' +
      'the dst reference remains permanently leaked.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'CPU 0                             CPU 1\n' +
      '__mkroute_output()\n' +
      '  find_exception() [fnheX]\n' +
      '                                  update_or_create_fnhe()\n' +
      '                                    fnhe_remove_oldest() [fnheX]\n' +
      '  rt_bind_exception() [bind dst]\n' +
      '                                  RCU callback [fnheX freed, dst leak]\n' +
      '\n' +
      'This issue manifests as a device reference count leak and a warning in\n' +
      'dmesg when unregistering the net device\n' +
      '\n' +
      '  unregister_netdevice waiting for sitX to become free. Usage count = N\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Ido Schimmel provided the simple test validation method [1].\n' +
      '\n' +
      "The fix clears 'oldest->fnhe_daddr' before calling fnhe_flush_routes().\n" +
      'Since rt_bind_exception() checks this field, setting it to zero prevents\n' +
      'the stale fnhe from being reused and bound to a new dst just before it\n' +
      'is freed.\n' +
      '\n' +
      '[1]\n' +
      'ip netns add ns1\n' +

      '    -A 198.51.100.1 -B 198.51.0.0/16 -t udp -p 1000 -c 0 -q \n' +
      'sleep 10\n' +
      'ip netns pids ns1 | xargs kill\n' +
      'ip netns del ns1 | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

      '\n' +
      'The problem can be reproduced as follow\n' +
      '\n' +
      '# echo "/media *(rw,no_root_squash,sync)" >> /etc/exports\n' +
      '# export -ra\n' +
      '# mount -o rw,nfsvers=4.2 127.0.0.1/media /tmpdir\n' +
      '# cd /opt/ltp\n' +
      '# ./runltp -d /tmpdir -s utimes01\n' +
      '# ./runltp -d /tmpdir -s utime06\n' +
      '\n' +
      "This issue occurs because nfs_setattr does not verify the inode's\n" +
      "UID against the caller's fsuid when delegated timestamps are\n" +
      'permitted for the inode.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'This patch adds the UID check and if it does not match then the\n' +
      'request is sent to the server for permission checking. | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

    title: 'CVE-2025-68245 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      'net netpoll fix incorrect ref...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68245',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 15:15:00 GMT',
    content: 'In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      'net netpoll fix incorrect refcount handling causing incorrect cleanup\n' +
      '\n' +
      'commit efa95b01da18 ("netpoll fix use after free") incorrectly\n' +
      'ignored the refcount and prematurely set dev->npinfo to NULL during\n' +
      'netpoll cleanup, leading to improper behavior and memory leaks.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Scenario causing lack of proper cleanup\n' +
      '\n' +
      '1) A netpoll is associated with a NIC (e.g., eth0) and netdev->npinfo is\n' +
      '   allocated, and refcnt = 1\n' +
      '   - Keep in mind that npinfo is shared among all netpoll instances. In\n' +
      '     this case, there is just one.\n' +
      '\n' +
      '2) Another netpoll is also associated with the same NIC and\n' +
      '   npinfo->refcnt += 1.\n' +
      '   - Now dev->npinfo->refcnt = 2\n' +
      '   - There is just one npinfo associated to the netdev.\n' +
      '\n' +
      '3) When the first netpolls goes to clean up\n' +
      '   - The first cleanup succeeds and clears np->dev->npinfo, ignoring\n' +
      '     refcnt.\n' +
      '     - It basically calls `RCU_INIT_POINTER(np->dev->npinfo, NULL)`\n' +
      '   - Set dev->npinfo = NULL, without proper cleanup\n' +
      '   - No ->ndo_netpoll_cleanup() is either called\n' +
      '\n' +
      '4) Now the second target tries to clean up\n' +
      '   - The second cleanup fails because np->dev->npinfo is already NULL.\n' +
      '     * In this case, ops->ndo_netpoll_cleanup() was never called, and\n' +
      '       the skb pool is not cleaned as well (for the second netpoll\n' +
      '       instance)\n' +
      '  - This leaks npinfo and skbpool skbs, which is clearly reported by\n' +
      '    kmemleak.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Revert commit efa95b01da18 ("netpoll fix use after free") and adds\n' +
      'clarifying comments emphasizing that npinfo cleanup should only happen\n' +
      'once the refcount reaches zero, ensuring stable and correct netpoll\n' +
      'behavior. | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

      '\n' +
      'vmw_balloon indicate success w...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68248',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 15:15:00 GMT',
    content: 'In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      'vmw_balloon indicate success when effectively deflating during migration\n' +
      '\n' +
      'When migrating a balloon page, we first deflate the old page to then\n' +
      'inflate the new page.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'However, if inflating the new page succeeded, we effectively deflated the\n' +
      'old page, reducing the balloon size.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'In that case, the migration actually worked similar to migrating+\n' +
      'immediately deflating the new page.  The old page will be freed back to\n' +
      'the buddy.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Right now, the core will leave the page be marked as isolated (as we\n' +
      'returned an error).  When later trying to putback that page, we will run\n' +
      'into the WARN_ON_ONCE() in balloon_page_putback().\n' +
      '\n' +
      'That handling was changed in commit 3544c4faccb8 ("mm/balloon_compaction\n' +
      'stop using __ClearPageMovable()") before that change, we would have\n' +
      'tolerated that way of handling it.\n' +
      '\n' +
      "To fix it, let's just return 0 in that case, making the core effectively\n" +
      'just clear the "isolated" flag + freeing it back to the buddy as if the\n' +
      'migration succeeded.  Note that the new page will also get freed when the\n' +
      'core puts the last reference.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Note that this also makes it all be more consistent we will no longer\n' +
      'unisolate the page in the balloon driver while keeping it marked as being\n' +
      'isolated in migration core.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'This was found by code inspection. | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

    content: 'In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      'hung_task fix warnings caused by unaligned lock pointers\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The blocker tracking mechanism assumes that lock pointers are at least\n' +
      '4-byte aligned to use their lower bits for type encoding.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'However, as reported by Eero Tamminen, some architectures like m68k\n' +
      'only guarantee 2-byte alignment of 32-bit values. This breaks the\n' +
      'assumption and causes two related WARN_ON_ONCE checks to trigger.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'To fix this, the runtime checks are adjusted to silently ignore any lock\n' +
      'that is not 4-byte aligned, effectively disabling the feature in such\n' +
      'cases and avoiding the related warnings.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Thanks to Geert Uytterhoeven for bisecting! | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

    title: 'CVE-2025-68259 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      "KVM SVM Don't skip unrelated ...",
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68259',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 15:15:00 GMT',
    content: 'In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      "KVM SVM Don't skip unrelated instruction if INT3/INTO is replaced\n" +
      '\n' +
      'When re-injecting a soft interrupt from an INT3, INT0, or (select) INTn\n' +
      'instruction, discard the exception and retry the instruction if the code\n' +
      'stream is changed (e.g. by a different vCPU) between when the CPU\n' +
      'executes the instruction and when KVM decodes the instruction to get the\n' +
      'next RIP.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'As effectively predicted by commit 6ef88d6e36c2 ("KVM SVM Re-inject\n' +
      'INT3/INTO instead of retrying the instruction"), failure to verify that\n' +
      'the correct INTn instruction was decoded can effectively clobber guest\n' +
      'state due to decoding the wrong instruction and thus specifying the\n' +
      'wrong next RIP.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The bug most often manifests as "Oops int3" panics on static branch\n' +
      'checks in Linux guests.  Enabling or disabling a static branch in Linux\n' +
      `uses the kernel's "text poke" code patching mechanism.  To modify code\n` +
      'while other CPUs may be executing that code, Linux (temporarily)\n' +
      'replaces the first byte of the original instruction with an int3 (opcode\n' +
      '0xcc), then patches in the new code stream except for the first byte,\n' +
      'and finally replaces the int3 with the first byte of the new code\n' +
      "stream.  If a CPU hits the int3, i.e. executes the code while it's being\n" +
      'modified, then the guest kernel must look up the RIP to determine how to\n' +
      'handle the #BP, e.g. by emulating the new instruction.  If the RIP is\n' +
      'incorrect, then this lookup fails and the guest kernel panics.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The bug reproduces almost instantly by hacking the guest kernel to\n' +
      'repeatedly check a static branch[1] while running a drgn script[2] on\n' +
      "the host to constantly swap out the memory containing the guest's TSS.\n" +
      '\n' +
      '[1] https//gist.github.com/osandov/44d17c51c28c0ac998ea0334edf90b5a\n' +
      '[2] https//gist.github.com/osandov/10e45e45afa29b11e0c7209247afc00b | Severity UNKNOWN  ',
    contentSnippet: 'In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      "KVM SVM Don't skip unrelated instruction if INT3/INTO is replaced\n" +
      '\n' +
      'When re-injecting a soft interrupt from an INT3, INT0, or (select) INTn\n' +
      'instruction, discard the exception and retry the instruction if the code\n' +
      'stream is changed (e.g. by a different vCPU) between when the CPU\n' +
      'executes the instruction and when KVM decodes the instruction to get the\n' +
      'next RIP.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'As effectively predicted by commit 6ef88d6e36c2 ("KVM SVM Re-inject\n' +
      'INT3/INTO instead of retrying the instruction"), failure to verify that\n' +
      'the correct INTn instruction was decoded can effectively clobber guest\n' +
      'state due to decoding the wrong instruction and thus specifying the\n' +
      'wrong next RIP.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The bug most often manifests as "Oops int3" panics on static branch\n' +
      'checks in Linux guests.  Enabling or disabling a static branch in Linux\n' +
      `uses the kernel's "text poke" code patching mechanism.  To modify code\n` +
      'while other CPUs may be executing that code, Linux (temporarily)\n' +
      'replaces the first byte of the original instruction with an int3 (opcode\n' +
      '0xcc), then patches in the new code stream except for the first byte,\n' +
      'and finally replaces the int3 with the first byte of the new code\n' +
      "stream.  If a CPU hits the int3, i.e. executes the code while it's being\n" +
      'modified, then the guest kernel must look up the RIP to determine how to\n' +
      'handle the #BP, e.g. by emulating the new instruction.  If the RIP is\n' +
      'incorrect, then this lookup fails and the guest kernel panics.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The bug reproduces almost instantly by hacking the guest kernel to\n' +
      'repeatedly check a static branch[1] while running a drgn script[2] on\n' +
      "the host to constantly swap out the memory containing the guest's TSS.\n" +
      '\n' +
      '[1] https//gist.github.com/osandov/44d17c51c28c0ac998ea0334edf90b5a\n' +
      '[2] https//gist.github.com/osandov/10e45e45afa29b11e0c7209247afc00b | Severity UNKNOWN',
    guid: 'CVE-2025-68259',
    isoDate: '2025-12-16T15:15:00.000Z'

      '\n' +
      'rust_binder fix race condition on death_list\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Rust Binder contains the following unsafe operation\n' +
      '\n' +
      '\t// SAFETY A `NodeDeath` is never inserted into the death list\n' +
      '\t// of any node other than its owner, so it is either in this\n' +
      '\t// death list or in no death list.\n' +
      '\tunsafe { node_inner.death_list.remove(self) }\n' +
      '\n' +
      'This operation is unsafe because when touching the prev/next pointers of\n' +
      'a list element, we have to ensure that no other thread is also touching\n' +
      'them in parallel. If the node is present in the list that `remove` is\n' +
      'called on, then that is fine because we have exclusive access to that\n' +
      "list. If the node is not in any list, then it's also ok. But if it's\n" +
      'present in a different list that may be accessed in parallel, then that\n' +
      'may be a data race on the prev/next pointers.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'And unfortunately that is exactly what is happening here. In\n' +
      'Noderelease, we\n' +
      '\n' +

      '\n' +
      'ksmbd ipc fix use-after-free in ipc_msg_send_request\n' +

      'ipc_msg_send_request() waits for a generic netlink reply using an\n' +

      '(handle_generic_event()/handle_response()) fills entry->response under\n' +

      '    ksmbd_rpc_open -> ksmbd_session_rpc_open [ksmbd]\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Fix by\n' +
      '- Taking ipc_msg_table_lock in ipc_msg_send_request() while validating\n' +
      '  entry->response, freeing it when invalid, and removing the entry from\n' +
      '  ipc_msg_table.\n' +

      '\n' +
      'ext4 refresh inline data size ...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68264',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 15:15:00 GMT',
    content: 'In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\n' +
      '\n' +
      'ext4 refresh inline data size before write operations\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The cached ei->i_inline_size can become stale between the initial size\n' +
      'check and when ext4_update_inline_data()/ext4_create_inline_data() use\n' +
      'it. Although ext4_get_max_inline_size() reads the correct value at the\n' +
      'time of the check, concurrent xattr operations can modify i_inline_size\n' +
      'before ext4_write_lock_xattr() is acquired.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'This causes ext4_update_inline_data() and ext4_create_inline_data() to\n' +
      'work with stale capacity values, leading to a BUG_ON() crash in\n' +
      'ext4_write_inline_data()\n' +
      '\n' +
      '  kernel BUG at fs/ext4/inline.c1331!\n' +
      '  BUG_ON(pos + len > EXT4_I(inode)->i_inline_size)\n' +
      '\n' +
      'The race window\n' +
      '1. ext4_get_max_inline_size() reads i_inline_size = 60 (correct)\n' +
      '2. Size check passes for 50-byte write\n' +
      '3. [Another thread adds xattr, i_inline_size changes to 40]\n' +
      '4. ext4_write_lock_xattr() acquires lock\n' +
      '5. ext4_update_inline_data() uses stale i_inline_size = 60\n' +
      '6. Attempts to write 50 bytes but only 40 bytes actually available\n' +
      '7. BUG_ON() triggers\n' +
      '\n' +
      'Fix this by recalculating i_inline_size via ext4_find_inline_data_nolock()\n' +
      'immediately after acquiring xattr_sem. This ensures ext4_update_inline_data()\n' +
      'and ext4_create_inline_data() work with current values that are protected\n' +
      'from concurrent modifications.\n' +
      '\n' +
      'This is similar to commit a54c4613dac1 ("ext4 fix race writing to an\n' +
      'inline_data file while its xattrs are changing") which fixed i_inline_off\n' +
      'staleness. This patch addresses the related i_inline_size staleness issue. | Severity UNKNOWN  ',

      'which causes the code to proceed with NULL clock pointers. The current\r\n' +
      'logic uses !PTR_ERR_OR_ZERO(cpu_clk) which evaluates to true for both\r\n' +
      'valid pointers and NULL, leading to potential NULL pointer dereference\r\n' +
      'in clk_get_rate().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Per include/linux/err.h documentation, PTR_ERR_OR_ZERO(ptr) returns\r\n' +
      '"The error code within @ptr if it is an error pointer 0 otherwise."\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This means PTR_ERR_OR_ZERO() returns 0 for both valid pointers AND NULL\r\n' +
      'pointers. Therefore !PTR_ERR_OR_ZERO(cpu_clk) evaluates to true (proceed)\r\n' +
      'when cpu_clk is either valid or NULL, causing clk_get_rate(NULL) to be\r\n' +
      'called when of_clk_get() returns NULL.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Replace with !IS_ERR_OR_NULL(cpu_clk) which only proceeds for valid\r\n' +
      'pointers, preventing potential NULL pointer dereference in clk_get_rate(). | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',
    contentSnippet: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +

  {
    title: 'CVE-2025-40350 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'net/mlx5e RX, Fix generating s...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-40350',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'net/mlx5e RX, Fix generating skb from non-linear xdp_buff for striding RQ\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'XDP programs can change the layout of an xdp_buff through\r\n' +
      'bpf_xdp_adjust_tail() and bpf_xdp_adjust_head(). Therefore, the driver\r\n' +
      'cannot assume the size of the linear data area nor fragments. Fix the\r\n' +
      'bug in mlx5 by generating skb according to xdp_buff after XDP programs\r\n' +
      'run.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Currently, when handling multi-buf XDP, the mlx5 driver assumes the\r\n' +
      'layout of an xdp_buff to be unchanged. That is, the linear data area\r\n' +
      'continues to be empty and fragments remain the same. This may cause\r\n' +
      'the driver to generate erroneous skb or triggering a kernel\r\n' +
      'warning. When an XDP program added linear data through\r\n' +
      'bpf_xdp_adjust_head(), the linear data will be ignored as\r\n' +
      'mlx5e_build_linear_skb() builds an skb without linear data and then\r\n' +
      'pull data from fragments to fill the linear data area. When an XDP\r\n' +
      'program has shrunk the non-linear data through bpf_xdp_adjust_tail(),\r\n' +
      'the delta passed to __pskb_pull_tail() may exceed the actual nonlinear\r\n' +
      'data size and trigger the BUG_ON in it.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'To fix the issue, first record the original number of fragments. If the\r\n' +
      'number of fragments changes after the XDP program runs, rewind the end\r\n' +
      'fragment pointer by the difference and recalculate the truesize. Then,\r\n' +
      'build the skb with the linear data area matching the xdp_buff. Finally,\r\n' +
      'only pull data in if there is non-linear data and fill the linear part\r\n' +
      'up to 256 bytes. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',
    contentSnippet: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'net/mlx5e RX, Fix generating skb from non-linear xdp_buff for striding RQ\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'XDP programs can change the layout of an xdp_buff through\r\n' +
      'bpf_xdp_adjust_tail() and bpf_xdp_adjust_head(). Therefore, the driver\r\n' +
      'cannot assume the size of the linear data area nor fragments. Fix the\r\n' +
      'bug in mlx5 by generating skb according to xdp_buff after XDP programs\r\n' +
      'run.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Currently, when handling multi-buf XDP, the mlx5 driver assumes the\r\n' +
      'layout of an xdp_buff to be unchanged. That is, the linear data area\r\n' +
      'continues to be empty and fragments remain the same. This may cause\r\n' +
      'the driver to generate erroneous skb or triggering a kernel\r\n' +
      'warning. When an XDP program added linear data through\r\n' +
      'bpf_xdp_adjust_head(), the linear data will be ignored as\r\n' +
      'mlx5e_build_linear_skb() builds an skb without linear data and then\r\n' +
      'pull data from fragments to fill the linear data area. When an XDP\r\n' +
      'program has shrunk the non-linear data through bpf_xdp_adjust_tail(),\r\n' +
      'the delta passed to __pskb_pull_tail() may exceed the actual nonlinear\r\n' +
      'data size and trigger the BUG_ON in it.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'To fix the issue, first record the original number of fragments. If the\r\n' +
      'number of fragments changes after the XDP program runs, rewind the end\r\n' +
      'fragment pointer by the difference and recalculate the truesize. Then,\r\n' +
      'build the skb with the linear data area matching the xdp_buff. Finally,\r\n' +
      'only pull data in if there is non-linear data and fill the linear part\r\n' +
      'up to 256 bytes. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',
    guid: 'CVE-2025-40350',
    isoDate: '2025-12-16T14:15:00.000Z'

    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-40353',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'arm64 mte Do not warn if the page is already tagged in copy_highpage()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The arm64 copy_highpage() assumes that the destination page is newly\r\n' +
      'allocated and not MTE-tagged (PG_mte_tagged unset) and warns\r\n' +
      'accordingly. However, following commit 060913999d7a ("mm migrate\r\n' +
      'support poisoned recover from migrate folio"), folio_mc_copy() is called\r\n' +
      'before __folio_migrate_mapping(). If the latter fails (-EAGAIN), the\r\n' +
      'copy will be done again to the same destination page. Since\r\n' +

      'copy_highpage() with a comment. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',
    contentSnippet: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'arm64 mte Do not warn if the page is already tagged in copy_highpage()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The arm64 copy_highpage() assumes that the destination page is newly\r\n' +
      'allocated and not MTE-tagged (PG_mte_tagged unset) and warns\r\n' +
      'accordingly. However, following commit 060913999d7a ("mm migrate\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'ceph fix multifs mds auth caps issue\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The mds auth caps check should also validate the\r\n' +
      'fsname along with the associated caps. Not doing\r\n' +
      'so would result in applying the mds auth caps of\r\n' +
      'one fs on to the other fs in a multifs ceph cluster.\r\n' +
      'The bug causes multiple issues w.r.t user\r\n' +
      'authentication, following is one such example.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Steps to Reproduce (on vstart cluster)\r\n' +
      "1. Create two file systems in a cluster, say 'fsname1' and 'fsname2'\r\n" +
      "2. Authorize read only permission to the user 'client.usr' on fs 'fsname1'\r\n" +
      '    $ceph fs authorize fsname1 client.usr / r\r\n' +
      "3. Authorize read and write permission to the same user 'client.usr' on fs 'fsname2'\r\n" +
      '    $ceph fs authorize fsname2 client.usr / rw\r\n' +
      '4. Update the keyring\r\n' +
      '    $ceph auth get client.usr >> ./keyring\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "With above permssions for the user 'client.usr', following is the\r\n" +
      'expectation.\r\n' +
      "  a. The 'client.usr' should be able to only read the contents\r\n" +
      "     and not allowed to create or delete files on file system 'fsname1'.\r\n" +
      "  b. The 'client.usr' should be able to read/write on file system 'fsname2'.\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      "But, with this bug, the 'client.usr' is allowed to read/write on file\r\n" +
      "system 'fsname1'. See below.\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      "5. Mount the file system 'fsname1' with the user 'client.usr'\r\n" +
      '     $sudo bin/mount.ceph usr@.fsname1=/ /kmnt_fsname1_usr/\r\n' +
      "6. Try creating a file on file system 'fsname1' with user 'client.usr'. This\r\n" +
      '   should fail but passes with this bug.\r\n' +
      '     $touch /kmnt_fsname1_usr/file1\r\n' +
      "7. Mount the file system 'fsname1' with the user 'client.admin' and create a\r\n" +
      '   file.\r\n' +
      '     $sudo bin/mount.ceph admin@.fsname1=/ /kmnt_fsname1_admin\r\n' +
      '     $echo "data" > /kmnt_fsname1_admin/admin_file1\r\n' +
      "8. Try removing an existing file on file system 'fsname1' with the user\r\n" +
      "   'client.usr'. This shoudn't succeed but succeeds with the bug.\r\n" +
      '     $rm -f /kmnt_fsname1_usr/admin_file1\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'For more information, please take a look at the corresponding mds/fuse patch\r\n' +
      'and tests added by looking into the tracker mentioned below.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'v2 Fix a possible null dereference in doutc\r\n' +
      "v3 Don't store fsname from mdsmap, validate against\r\n" +
      "    ceph_mount_options's fsname and use it\r\n" +
      'v4 Code refactor, better warning message and\r\n' +
      '    fix possible compiler warning\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '[ Slava.Dubeyko "fsname check failed" -> "fsname mismatch" ] | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',

    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68169',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'netpoll Fix deadlock in memory allocation under spinlock\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Fix a AA deadlock in refill_skbs() where memory allocation while holding\r\n' +
      'skb_pool->lock can trigger a recursive lock acquisition attempt.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The deadlock scenario occurs when the system is under severe memory\r\n' +
      'pressure\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '1. refill_skbs() acquires skb_pool->lock (spinlock)\r\n' +
      '2. alloc_skb() is called while holding the lock\r\n' +
      '3. Memory allocator fails and calls slab_out_of_memory()\r\n' +
      '4. This triggers printk() for the OOM warning\r\n' +
      '5. The console output path calls netpoll_send_udp()\r\n' +
      '6. netpoll_send_udp() attempts to acquire the same skb_pool->lock\r\n' +
      '7. Deadlock the lock is already held by the same CPU\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Call stack\r\n' +
      '  refill_skbs()\r\n' +
      '    spin_lock_irqsave(skb_pool->lock)    - lock acquired\r\n' +
      '    __alloc_skb()\r\n' +
      '      kmem_cache_alloc_node_noprof()\r\n' +
      '        slab_out_of_memory()\r\n' +
      '          printk()\r\n' +
      '            console_flush_all()\r\n' +
      '              netpoll_send_udp()\r\n' +
      '                skb_dequeue()\r\n' +
      '                  spin_lock_irqsave(skb_pool->lock)     - deadlock attempt\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This bug was exposed by commit 248f6571fd4c51 ("netpoll Optimize skb\r\n' +
      'refilling on critical path") which removed refill_skbs() from the\r\n' +
      'critical path (where nested printk was being deferred), letting nested\r\n' +
      'printk being called from inside refill_skbs()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Refactor refill_skbs() to never allocate memory while holding\r\n' +
      'the spinlock.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Another possible solution to fix this problem is protecting the\r\n' +
      'refill_skbs() from nested printks, basically calling\r\n' +
      'printk_deferred_{enter,exit}() in refill_skbs(), then, any nested\r\n' +
      'pr_warn() would be deferred.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'I prefer this approach, given I _think_ it might be a good idea to move\r\n' +
      'the alloc_skb() from GFP_ATOMIC to GFP_KERNEL in the future, so, having\r\n' +
      'the alloc_skb() outside of the lock will be necessary step.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'There is a possible TOCTOU issue when checking for the pool length, and\r\n' +
      'queueing the new allocated skb, but, this is not an issue, given that\r\n' +
      'an extra SKB in the pool is harmless and it will be eventually used. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',

  {
    title: 'CVE-2025-68179 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      's390 Disable ARCH_WANT_OPTIMIZ...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68179',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      's390 Disable ARCH_WANT_OPTIMIZE_HUGETLB_VMEMMAP\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'As reported by Luiz Capitulino enabling HVO on s390 leads to reproducible\r\n' +
      'crashes. The problem is that kernel page tables are modified without\r\n' +
      'flushing corresponding TLB entries.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Even if it looks like the empty flush_tlb_all() implementation on s390 is\r\n' +
      'the problem, it is actually a different problem on s390 it is not allowed\r\n' +
      'to replace an active/valid page table entry with another valid page table\r\n' +
      'entry without the detour over an invalid entry. A direct replacement may\r\n' +
      'lead to random crashes and/or data corruption.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In order to invalidate an entry special instructions have to be used\r\n' +
      '(e.g. ipte or idte). Alternatively there are also special instructions\r\n' +
      'available which allow to replace a valid entry with a different valid\r\n' +
      'entry (e.g. crdte or cspg).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Given that the HVO code currently does not provide the hooks to allow for\r\n' +
      'an implementation which is compliant with the s390 architecture\r\n' +
      'requirements, disable ARCH_WANT_OPTIMIZE_HUGETLB_VMEMMAP again, which is\r\n' +
      'basically a revert of the original patch which enabled it. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',
    contentSnippet: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      's390 Disable ARCH_WANT_OPTIMIZE_HUGETLB_VMEMMAP\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'As reported by Luiz Capitulino enabling HVO on s390 leads to reproducible\r\n' +
      'crashes. The problem is that kernel page tables are modified without\r\n' +
      'flushing corresponding TLB entries.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Even if it looks like the empty flush_tlb_all() implementation on s390 is\r\n' +
      'the problem, it is actually a different problem on s390 it is not allowed\r\n' +
      'to replace an active/valid page table entry with another valid page table\r\n' +
      'entry without the detour over an invalid entry. A direct replacement may\r\n' +
      'lead to random crashes and/or data corruption.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In order to invalidate an entry special instructions have to be used\r\n' +
      '(e.g. ipte or idte). Alternatively there are also special instructions\r\n' +
      'available which allow to replace a valid entry with a different valid\r\n' +
      'entry (e.g. crdte or cspg).\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      "ima don't clear IMA_DIGSIG flag when setting or removing non-IMA xattr\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      'Currently when both IMA and EVM are in fix mode, the IMA signature will\r\n' +
      'be reset to IMA hash if a program first stores IMA signature in\r\n' +
      'security.ima and then writes/removes some other security xattr for the\r\n' +
      'file.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'For example, on Fedora, after booting the kernel with "ima_appraise=fix\r\n' +
      'evm=fix ima_policy=appraise_tcb" and installing rpm-plugin-ima,\r\n' +
      'installing/reinstalling a package will not make good reference IMA\r\n' +
      'signature generated. Instead IMA hash is generated,\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '    # getfattr -m - -d -e hex /usr/bin/bash\r\n' +
      '    # file usr/bin/bash\r\n' +
      '    security.ima=0x0404...\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This happens because when setting security.selinux, the IMA_DIGSIG flag\r\n' +
      'that had been set early was cleared. As a result, IMA hash is generated\r\n' +
      'when the file is closed.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +

    content: '![CDATA[![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'media imon make send_packet() more robust\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'syzbot is reporting that imon has three problems which result in\r\n' +
      'hung tasks due to forever holding device lock [1].\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'First problem is that when usb_rx_callback_intf0() once got -EPROTO error\r\n' +
      'after ictx->dev_present_intf0 became true, usb_rx_callback_intf0()\r\n' +
      'resubmits urb after printk(), and resubmitted urb causes\r\n' +
      'usb_rx_callback_intf0() to again get -EPROTO error. This results in\r\n' +
      'printk() flooding (RCU stalls).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Alan Stern commented [2] that\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "  In theory it's okay to resubmit _if_ the driver has a robust\r\n" +
      '  error-recovery scheme (such as giving up after some fixed limit on the\r\n' +
      '  number of errors or after some fixed time has elapsed, perhaps with a\r\n' +
      "  time delay to prevent a flood of errors).  Most drivers don't bother to\r\n" +
      '  do this they simply give up right away.  This makes them more\r\n' +
      '  vulnerable to short-term noise interference during USB transfers, but in\r\n' +
      "  reality such interference is quite rare.  There's nothing really wrong\r\n" +
      '  with giving up right away.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'but imon has a poor error-recovery scheme which just retries forever\r\n' +
      'this behavior should be fixed.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "Since I'm not sure whether it is safe for imon users to give up upon any\r\n" +
      'error code, this patch takes care of only union of error codes chosen from\r\n' +
      'modules in drivers/media/rc/ directory which handle -EPROTO error (i.e.\r\n' +
      'ir_toy, mceusb and igorplugusb).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Second problem is that when usb_rx_callback_intf0() once got -EPROTO error\r\n' +
      'before ictx->dev_present_intf0 becomes true, usb_rx_callback_intf0() always\r\n' +
      `resubmits urb due to commit 8791d63af0cf ("[media] imon don't wedge\r\n` +
      'hardware after early callbacks"). Move the ictx->dev_present_intf0 test\r\n' +
      `introduced by commit 6f6b90c9231a ("[media] imon don't parse scancodes\r\n` +
      'until intf configured") to immediately before imon_incoming_packet(), or\r\n' +
      'the first problem explained above happens without printk() flooding (i.e.\r\n' +
      'hung task).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Third problem is that when usb_rx_callback_intf0() is not called for some\r\n' +
      'reason (e.g. flaky hardware the reproducer for this problem sometimes\r\n' +
      'prevents usb_rx_callback_intf0() from being called),\r\n' +
      'wait_for_completion_interruptible() in send_packet() never returns (i.e.\r\n' +
      'hung task). As a workaround for such situation, change send_packet() to\r\n' +
      'wait for completion with timeout of 10 seconds. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>]]>',
